<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 3.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><font style="font-size:10.0pt;">NOTICE
OF ANNUAL </font>MEETING OF STOCKHOLDERS</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 14.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">TO BE
HELD ON WEDNESDAY, OCTOBER 8, 2003</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 14.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">To the
Stockholders of AAR CORP.:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Annual Meeting of Stockholders of AAR CORP. for
the year 2003 will be held at AAR CORP.&#146;s headquarters, One AAR Place, 1100
North Wood Dale Road, Wood Dale, Illinois, on Wednesday, October&nbsp;8, 2003,
at 10:00&nbsp;A.M. (Chicago time). At the meeting, stockholders will act on the
following matters:</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 20.15pt;text-indent:-20.15pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">1.</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>To elect three Class&nbsp;I
directors to serve until the 2006 Annual Meeting of Stockholders; and</p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 20.15pt;text-indent:-20.15pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2.</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>To
transact any other business that may properly come before the 2003 Annual
Meeting.</p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 24.0pt 250.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">By Order of the Board of Directors</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 250.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">HOWARD A. PULSIFER<br>
<i><font style="font-style:italic;">Secretary</font></i></font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">August&nbsp;27, 2003</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">YOUR
VOTE IS IMPORTANT</font></b></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;line-height:12.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><b><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:9.0pt;">PLEASE DATE AND SIGN THE ENCLOSED
FORM&nbsp;OF PROXY AND RETURN IT IN THE ENCLOSED STAMPED, ADDRESSED ENVELOPE,
OR SUBMIT YOUR PROXY BY TELEPHONE OR THE INTERNET SO THAT IF YOU ARE UNABLE TO
ATTEND THE MEETING, YOUR SHARES MAY&nbsp;NEVERTHELESS BE VOTED. NO POSTAGE IS
REQUIRED FOR MAILING IN THE UNITED STATES.</font></b></p>


 <p style="line-height:9.0pt;margin:24.0pt 18.0pt .0001pt 0pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
</div><br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 4.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">PROXY STATEMENT</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">ANNUAL MEETING OF STOCKHOLDERS<br>
October&nbsp;8, 2003</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><a name="solicitation"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">I. SOLICITATION</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This Proxy Statement and the
enclosed proxy card were mailed to stockholders on or about August&nbsp;27,
2003, in connection with the solicitation of proxies by the Board of Directors
of the Company to be used at the 2003 Annual Meeting (&#147;Annual Meeting&#148;).</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">If you are a stockholder of record (i.e., you hold
your shares in your own name other than through a broker, bank or other
nominee), you are encouraged to submit your proxy vote either by telephone or
the Internet. This will eliminate the need to sign, date and return your proxy
card. To submit your proxy by telephone or the Internet you will be required to
enter the control number assigned to you and imprinted on your proxy card
accompanying this Proxy Statement. The vote by telephone and vote by Internet
can be accessed 24 hours a day, seven days a week until the day prior to the
Annual Meeting.</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.25pt;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-family:Symbol;font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font style="font-weight:bold;">To submit your proxy vote by telephone:</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 50.4pt;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"><img width="7" height="7" src="da3744image004.gif">&#160; <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">using
a touch-tone phone, call 1-877-PRX-VOTE (1-877-779-8683) toll-free and follow
the voice prompts</font></b></font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.25pt;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-family:Symbol;font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font style="font-weight:bold;">To submit your proxy vote by internet:</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 50.4pt;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"><img width="7" height="7" src="da3744image004.gif">&#160; <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Log
onto internet website at </font><u>http://www.eproxyvote.com/air</u> and enter your voter control number on your
proxy card and mark the appropriate boxes to enter voting instructions</b></font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">If you are a street-name
stockholder (i.e., you hold your shares through a broker, bank or other
nominee), you will receive instructions from your broker, bank or other nominee
describing how you may vote your shares.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">You may change your vote at any
time before your proxy is exercised, but only by voting in person at the Annual
Meeting, submitting another proxy by telephone, the Internet, or delivering a
later dated, signed proxy to the Secretary of the Company.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Proxies will be voted in accordance with instructions
on the proxy. If no instructions are specified, the named proxy holders will
vote FOR the election of the nominees for Class&nbsp;I director designated by
the Board and upon any other matter that may properly come before the Annual
Meeting in their discretion and best judgment. The Board may nominate another
person if any nominee becomes unavailable for election for any reason prior to
the Annual Meeting vote. In that event, the named proxy holders will vote for
that other person.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The cost of the solicitation
of proxies will be paid by the Company. The Company has engaged D. F. King&nbsp;&amp;
Co., 77 Water Street, New York, New York, to aid in the solicitation of proxies
at a total estimated cost of $8,000, plus reasonable out-of-pocket expenses. D.
F. King&nbsp;&amp; Co. may solicit </font></p>

<font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;">
 <p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;line-height:150%;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;">1</p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">proxies by mail, telephone,
facsimile, e-mail, or in person. Certain officers, directors and employees of
the Company may also solicit proxies.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><a name="recorddate"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">II. RECORD
DATE AND VOTING AT THE ANNUAL MEETING</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Stockholders
owning common stock of the Company (&#147;Common Stock&#148;) outstanding at the close of
business on the record date, August&nbsp;13, 2003, may vote at the Annual
Meeting. On that date, 31,849,811&nbsp;shares of Common Stock were outstanding.
Stockholders will have one vote on each matter to be voted on for each share
held on the record date. Shares cannot be voted unless the owner is present at
the Annual Meeting in person or by proxy. A majority of the outstanding shares
of Common Stock entitled to vote, present in person or represented by proxy,
will constitute a quorum. Votes cast in person or by proxy will be tabulated by
the inspectors of election appointed for the Annual Meeting. The inspectors of
election will treat directions to withhold authority, abstentions and broker
non-votes as shares that are present and entitled to vote for purposes of
determining a quorum. Directions to withhold authority will have no effect on
the election of directors, because directors are elected by a plurality of
votes cast. Abstentions and broker non-votes will be disregarded for purposes
of determining whether a matter has been approved, because they are not
considered votes cast. It is not anticipated that there will be any broker
non-votes on the election of directors since brokers will have discretion to
vote on this proposal.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><a name="corpgov"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">III. CORPORATE
GOVERNANCE INFORMATION</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Information about the Company&#146;s
corporate governance practices and Board Committee charters is available on the
Company&#146;s web site (www.aarcorp.com) by clicking on the section titled &#147;Investor
Relations&#148; and subsection &#147;Corporate Governance.&#148;&#160; The display includes the Company&#146;s:</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.25pt;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-family:Symbol;font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Corporate

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.25pt;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-family:Symbol;font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Code of

and Governance Committee Charter</p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s <i><font style="font-style:italic;">Code of Business Ethics and Conduct</font></i> adopted by the Board of
Directors applies to employees and directors of the Company, including the
Chief Executive Officer, the Chief Financial Officer and the Chief Accounting
Officer and Controller.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Information concerning insider
transactions in the Company&#146;s securities (SEC Section&nbsp;16a Forms 3, 4 and
5) is also available on the Company&#146;s web site by clicking on &#147;Investor
Relations&#148; and &#147;Insider Trading&#148; (to view actual Forms 3, 4 or 5, click on the
Insider Trading link to the SEC filings).</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company maintains an Ethics
Assist Line through a third-party provider to receive confidential or anonymous
complaints, information, suggestions or recommendations, anonymously or
otherwise, concerning the Company, its officers, directors and employees,
policies, procedures, employment and business practices, accounting or audit
matters, financial reporting or compliance with other Company policies or
applicable regulatory or legal requirements.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><a name="brddir"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">IV.
BOARD OF DIRECTORS</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Restated Certificate of Incorporation and By-Laws of the Company provide that
the Board shall consist of between three and fifteen directors. The exact
number of directors is set from time to time by the Board. The number of
directors is presently set at eight. The members of the Board are divided into
three classes:&#160; Class&nbsp;I (three
directors), Class&nbsp;II (two directors) and Class&nbsp;III (three directors).
&#160;One class is elected each year for a
three-year term.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During
the fiscal year ended May&nbsp;31, 2003 (&#147;Fiscal 2003&#148;), the Board held five
meetings. All of the incumbent directors attended 100% of the aggregate
meetings of the Board and of the committees on which they served during Fiscal
2003, except one director was unable to attend one of the five Audit Committee
meetings due to illness.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 1.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><a name="retired"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">RETIRED DIRECTORS</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Edgar D.
Jannotta retired from the Board effective November&nbsp;30, 2002, and Howard B.
Bernick retired from the Board effective December&nbsp;18, 2002. Mr.&nbsp;Jannotta
served as a director for 38 years and Mr.&nbsp;Bernick served for 8 years. The
Board, on behalf of the Company and its stockholders, expresses its utmost
appreciation to each of them for their years of dedicated service as a
director.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 1.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><a name="committees"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">BOARD COMMITTEES</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Board has an Audit Committee, a Compensation Committee, a Nomination and
Governance Committee, and an Executive Committee.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 1.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Audit Committee</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Audit Committee is comprised entirely of independent directors (as defined by
applicable Securities and Exchange Commission (&#147;SEC&#148;) regulations and New York
Stock Exchange (&#147;NYSE&#148;) rules). Its members are A. Robert Abboud (Chairman),
James G. Brocksmith,&nbsp;Jr., James E. Goodwin, and Joel D. Spungin. The Board
of Directors has determined that more than one member of the Audit Committee is
a financial expert, including Mr.&nbsp;Abboud. The Audit Committee acts
pursuant to its written charter adopted by the Board of Directors. The charter
was reviewed by the Audit Committee at its March, 2003 meeting and amended by
the Board of Directors upon Audit Committee recommendation, to clarify the
Audit Committee&#146;s role and responsibilities and incorporate other new
requirements under the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002, and related final and
proposed SEC regulations and NYSE rules&nbsp;(a copy of the Audit Committee
charter, as revised, is attached to this proxy statement as Appendix 1). The
Audit Committee performs the functions described in its charter and, among
other things, approves and engages the independent auditors who audit the
Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements, pre-approves all non-audit/audit
related services furnished by the independent auditors, maintains communication
between the Board and its independent auditors, monitors performance of the
independent auditors, has oversight of and reviews the Company&#146;s financial reporting
process and practices, has oversight of and reviews the adequacy of financial
accounting controls, disclosure controls and the organization and performance
of the Company&#146;s internal systems of audit, reviews the scope and results of
audits, and meets with the independent auditors and internal auditors without
members of management present. The Audit Committee held five meetings during
Fiscal 2003.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 1.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Compensation Committee</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Compensation Committee is comprised entirely of independent directors (as defined
by NYSE rules). Its members are James G. Brocksmith,&nbsp;Jr. (Chairman), A.
Robert Abboud, Ronald R. Fogleman, and Joel D. Spungin. The Compensation
Committee performs the functions described in its written charter and, among
other things, reviews and approves compensation policies and practices for all
elected corporate officers, fixes the compensation of the President and Chief </font></p>

<font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;">
 <p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;line-height:9.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;">3</p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">

<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=6,EFW="2115196",CP="AAR CORP",DN="1",CHK=915002,FOLIO='3',FILE="DISK027:[03CHI4.03CHI3744.EDGAR]DE3744.CHC",USER="AGAETZ",CD='Aug 11 15:48 2003' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Executive
Officer, evaluates the Chief Executive Officer&#146;s performance, and administers
the Chief Executive Officer&#146;s long-term incentive program, the annual incentive
compensation programs for other officers, and the AAR CORP. Stock Benefit Plan.
The Compensation Committee held three meetings during Fiscal 2003.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 1.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Nomination and Governance Committee</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Nomination and Governance Committee is comprised entirely of independent
directors (as defined by NYSE rules). Its members are James E. Goodwin
(Chairman), Ronald R. Fogleman and Marc J. Walfish. The Nomination and
Governance Committee is responsible for both nominating and governance
functions as described in its charter. Among other things, it oversees the
composition, structure and evaluation of the Board and its committees, develops
and recommends corporate governance guidelines for Board approval, monitors and
screens directors for independence and recommends to the Board qualified
candidates for election as directors and to serve on Board committees. The
Nomination and Governance Committee will consider director candidates
recommended by stockholders. Stockholders may submit a recommendation to the
Nomination and Governance Committee for consideration with respect to the
Annual Meeting of Stockholders for the year 2004 by writing to the Secretary,
AAR CORP., One AAR Place, 1100 N. Wood Dale Road, Wood Dale, Illinois 60191. To
be considered, recommendations must be received prior to April&nbsp;11, 2004,
must state the reasons for the recommendation and contain the full name and
address of each proposed nominee, as well as a brief biographical history
setting forth past and present directorships, employment and occupations, and
any other qualifications. Recommendations must also include a statement
indicating that the proposed nominees have consented to being named in the
proxy statement and to serve if elected. The Nomination and Governance
Committee held one meeting during Fiscal 2003.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 1.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Executive Committee</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Executive Committee is comprised of Ira A. Eichner (Chairman), David P. Storch
and A. Robert Abboud. Mr.&nbsp;Abboud is an independent director (as defined by
NYSE rules). The Executive Committee acts pursuant to its written charter
adopted by the Board of Directors and is authorized to meet between meetings of
the Board of Directors and exercise certain powers of the Board with respect to
urgent matters or other matters referred to it by the Board for deliberation or
action, subject to limitations imposed by the Committee&#146;s charter, the Board,
applicable law and the Company&#146;s By-Laws. The Executive Committee held one
meeting during Fiscal 2003.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 1.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><a name="compensation"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">DIRECTORS&#146; COMPENSATION</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Each
director who is not an officer or employee of the Company or any subsidiary (&#147;Eligible
Director&#148;) receives an annual retainer of $35,000, a fee of $2,500 for
attendance at each meeting of the Board or of any Board committee attended in
person ($1,250 per meeting for telephonic Board and Committee meetings), plus
reimbursement of expenses. The Chairman of the Board and each committee
chairman receive an additional $5,000 annual retainer. Each Eligible Director
may elect to defer receipt of the annual retainer and meeting fees pursuant to
the Company&#146;s Nonemployee Directors&#146; Deferred Compensation Plan (the &#147;Plan&#148;). Deferred
retainer fees are converted into stock units equivalent to shares of Common
Stock and deferred meeting fees are credited with interest quarterly based on
the 10-year United States Treasury Bond rate. Distributions under the Plan
occur upon termination of service on the Board and on the happening of certain
other events as specified in the Plan.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 5.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
addition, each Eligible Director, upon being elected a director, receives term
life insurance coverage of $200,000, and is eligible to receive discretionary
stock option grants from time to time, as may be determined by the Board, of
Common Stock under the AAR CORP. Stock Benefit Plan. It is anticipated that
grants to directors will be made annually. Typically, such options expire ten
years from the date of grant and become exercisable in 25% increments on each
anniversary grant date at the closing New York Stock Exchange (&#147;NYSE&#148;) price on
the date of grant. On July&nbsp;21, 2003, each director was granted an option
for 3,500 shares at an exercise price of $6.96 per share.</font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;line-height:9.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;">4</p>
</div><br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">

<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=7,EFW="2115196",CP="AAR CORP",DN="1",CHK=838882,FOLIO='4',FILE="DISK027:[03CHI4.03CHI3744.EDGAR]DE3744.CHC",USER="AGAETZ",CD='Aug 11 15:48 2003' -->



<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The AAR CORP. Directors&#146;
Retirement Plan was terminated effective April&nbsp;10, 2001. Any Eligible
Director who was a director on the plan&#146;s effective date of termination or a
retired director then receiving benefits under the plan will continue to
receive benefits pursuant to the terms of the plan as the plan was in effect
and applicable to such participant on the earlier of the date of plan
termination or date of retirement. Benefits are paid upon retirement from the
Board on or after age 65 if such director has completed at least five years of
service as a director. Benefits are paid quarterly in cash in an amount equal
to 25% of the annual retainer payable to an active eligible director and are
paid for a period equal to the total number of years of service as a director
to a maximum of ten years or until death. Continuing liabilities under the AAR
CORP. Directors&#146; Retirement Plan are unfunded. As of May&nbsp;31, 2003, five
former directors were receiving retirement benefits under the plan.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Directors who are officers or
employees of the Company or any subsidiary receive no additional compensation
for service on the Board or any of its committees.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><a name="relationships"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">CERTAIN
RELATIONSHIPS AND RELATED TRANSACTIONS</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Mr.&nbsp;Walfish, a director of
the Company, is a partner of William Blair&nbsp;&amp; Company, L.L.C. (&#147;William
Blair&#148;). William Blair, from time to time, has rendered investment banking
services to the Company and received customary compensation for those services.
William Blair last rendered services to the Company in Fiscal Year 2002. The
Company may engage William Blair for additional services in the future.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Mr.&nbsp;Eichner,
a director of the Company and Chairman of the Board, provided consulting
services to the Company pursuant to a four year consulting agreement that
expired on May&nbsp;31, 2003 under which he received a quarterly consulting fee
in the amount of $25,000. During Fiscal 2003, Mr.&nbsp;Eichner received
$100,000 in consulting fees.</font></p>

<p style="font-size:12.0pt;font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><a name="proposal1"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:12.0pt;">V. PROPOSAL 1</font></b></a><font face="Times New Roman"><br>
</font>ELECTION OF DIRECTORS</p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Board of Directors is presently divided into three
classes, each having three-year terms that expire in successive years. The
Board of Directors has nominated three directors to be elected in Class&nbsp;I
at the Annual Meeting, each to serve a three-year term expiring at the 2006
Annual Meeting or until the individual is succeeded by another qualified
director who has been duly elected.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The nominees for Director in Class&nbsp;I
this year are <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Joel D. Spungin, James G. Brocksmith,&nbsp;Jr.
and David P. Storch</font></b>.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Information about the nominees,
and continuing directors whose terms expire in future years, is set forth in Section&nbsp;VI
below beginning on page&nbsp;6.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Each
nominee is currently serving as a director of the Company. The Board expects
all nominees to serve if elected as directors. If any of them should become
unavailable to serve as a director for any reason prior to the Annual Meeting,
the Board may substitute another person as nominee. In such event, the proxy
holders, in their discretion, will vote the shares for which they serve as
proxy for another person nominated by the Board unless the Board reduces the
number of directors to be elected. Under Delaware law and the Company&#146;s
By-Laws, the nominees for director who individually receive the greatest number
of votes shall be elected directors of the Company.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><b><i><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;font-style:italic;">THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS RECOMMENDS
THAT<br>
STOCKHOLDERS VOTE <u>FOR</u> ALL NOMINEES</font></i></b></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;line-height:9.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;">5</p>
</div><br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><a name="securityownership"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman"><font style="font-size:12.0pt;">VII</font>.
SECURITY OWNERSHIP OF MANAGEMENT AND OTHERS</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The following tables show the shares of Common Stock
beneficially owned, as of July&nbsp;31, 2003, by (i)&nbsp;each current director
and nominee for election to the Board, (ii)&nbsp;each executive officer named
in the Summary Compensation Table, (iii)&nbsp;all directors and executive
officers of the Company as a group, and (iv)&nbsp;each beneficial owner of more
than 5% of the outstanding shares of Common Stock. Except as noted, the nature
of beneficial ownership for shares shown in the tables is sole voting and/or
investment power.</font></p>

identified person that may be acquired within sixty days of July 31, 2003
through the exercise of stock options:&#160;
Mr.&nbsp;Brocksmith, 5,000 shares; Mr.&nbsp;Clark, 59,045 shares; Mr.&nbsp;Eichner,
240,964 shares; Mr.&nbsp;Fogleman, 5,000 shares; Mr.&nbsp;Goodwin, 2,500; Mr.&nbsp;Pulsifer,
77,720 shares; Mr.&nbsp;Romenesko, 110,442 shares; Mr.&nbsp;Sharp, 25,400
shares; and Mr.&nbsp;Storch, 1,400,254 shares; and all directors and officers
as a group, 1,926,325 shares.</font></p>

disclaims beneficial ownership.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 20.15pt;text-indent:-20.15pt;"><sup><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:8.0pt;">3</font></sup><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="1" style="font-size:8.0pt;">Includes 25,686 shares beneficially owned

shares), as to which Mr.&nbsp;Storch disclaims beneficial ownership.</font></p>

 <p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;line-height:9.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;">8</p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">

<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=11,EFW="2115196",CP="AAR CORP",DN="1",CHK=981937,FOLIO='8',FILE="DISK027:[03CHI4.03CHI3744.EDGAR]DK3744.CHC",USER="AGAETZ",CD='Aug 12 16:32 2003' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><a name="section16"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">SECTION&nbsp;16(a)&nbsp;BENEFICIAL
OWNERSHIP REPORTING COMPLIANCE</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Based solely upon a review of
Securities and Exchange Commission Forms 3, 4 and 5 and upon related written
representations furnished to the Company with respect to its most recent fiscal
year, no person who, at any time during the fiscal year, was a director,
officer or beneficial owner of more than ten percent of any class of equity securities
of the Company registered pursuant to Section&nbsp;12 of the Securities
Exchange Act of 1934, as amended (&#147;Exchange Act&#148;), failed to file on a timely
basis reports required by Section&nbsp;16(a)&nbsp;of the Exchange Act during
the most recent fiscal year.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><a name="execcomp"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">VIII. EXECUTIVE
COMPENSATION AND OTHER INFORMATION</font></b></a></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><a name="compcomm"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">COMPENSATION COMMITTEE&#146;S
REPORT ON EXECUTIVE COMPENSATION</font></b></a></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">General</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s executive
compensation program is structured and administered by the Compensation
Committee of the Board of Directors. The Compensation Committee is comprised of
the four individuals listed below, all of whom have been determined by the
Board of Directors to be independent directors of the Company within the
meaning of applicable SEC regulations and NYSE listing company rules.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The executive compensation
program is designed to enable the Company to attract, motivate and retain
talented executives capable of achieving strategic business initiatives and to
reward them for their achievement. It is designed to complement the Company&#146;s
short-term and long-term business objectives and to focus executives&#146; efforts
on fulfilling these objectives. The program consists of three elements:&#160; (i)&nbsp;base salaries which are generally
set between the median and third quartile salary level of comparable positions
in similar companies, adjusted up or down to reflect individual
responsibilities, performance and other relevant factors; (ii)&nbsp;annual
variable incentive opportunities paid in cash and stock based on individual
contribution and performance; and (iii)&nbsp;long-term incentive opportunities,
in the form of stock options and restricted stock awards.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Total compensation opportunities
for each executive are intended to be competitive with those offered by other
companies competing for talent in the Company&#146;s employment market. In designing
and administering the individual elements of the executive compensation program
for each executive, the Compensation Committee strives to balance short- and
long-term incentive objectives and employ prudent judgment in establishing base
salary levels and performance criteria, evaluating performance and determining
actual incentive payments. To ensure competitiveness and reasonableness of the
Compensation Committee&#146;s compensation decisions, independent compensation
consulting firms are retained periodically to advise the Compensation Committee
in connection with both the design and implementation of the various elements
of the program and the level of individual executive participation. The Company
uses competitive compensation analyses by independent consultants to ensure
that the President and Chief Executive Officer&#146;s and other executive officers&#146;
base salaries and total compensation are at an appropriate competitive level
relative to compensation for such positions at other companies in the relevant
employment market. Generally, as an executive&#146;s level of responsibility
increases, a greater percentage of total compensation is based on performance,
and the mix of total compensation shifts toward stock, thereby aligning the
long-term interest of senior executives with those of stockholders.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;line-height:9.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;">9</p>
</div><br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">

<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=12,EFW="2115196",CP="AAR CORP",DN="1",CHK=248197,FOLIO='9',FILE="DISK027:[03CHI4.03CHI3744.EDGAR]DK3744.CHC",USER="AGAETZ",CD='Aug 12 16:32 2003' -->



<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Base
Salaries</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Base
salary levels of all elected corporate officers, including the President and
Chief Executive Officer, are reviewed annually by the Compensation Committee
and may be adjusted depending upon the executive&#146;s qualifications,
responsibilities, assessed performance contribution, tenure in the Company and
in the position held, and competitive salary considerations relative to similar
positions at other companies competing for talent in the Company&#146;s employment
market. Effective October&nbsp;1, 2001, as part of a Company-wide cost
reduction effort following the terrorists attacks of September&nbsp;11, 2001,
and the resulting adverse impact on the aviation industry, the salaries of all
elected officers of the Company were temporarily reduced by 5-10% based on
salary level. The salary level for the President and Chief Executive Officer
and the Executive Vice President and Chief Operating Officer were each
temporarily reduced 10% effective October&nbsp;1, 2001. Effective April&nbsp;29,
2002, salary reductions were reinstated up to 5% of salary for all employees. The
base salaries of the President and Chief Executive Officer and other executive
officers named in the Summary Compensation Table were not changed in Fiscal
2003 and reflect the factors referred to above.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Annual
Incentive Opportunities</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The President and Chief
Executive Officer has an annual performance-based incentive bonus opportunity
of up to 150% of his base salary. Twenty percent of his incentive bonus is
payable in restricted stock that vests ratably in equal amounts over a three
year period. The percentage incentive bonus opportunity for other executive
positions varies depending on their responsibility level.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In 2002,
the Company&#146;s stockholders approved the &#147;AAR CORP. Section&nbsp;162(m)
Performance Based Annual Cash Bonus Program.&#148;&#160;
Under that program, each fiscal year the Compensation Committee
establishes specific annual cash bonus performance goals intended to meet the
requirements of Section&nbsp;162(m) of the Internal Revenue Code (&#147;IRC&#148;), for
the President and Chief Executive Officer of the Company and certain other
executive officers of the Company. These goals focus on two categories:&#160; income and balance sheet management. The
importance and weighting of these two categories is established each year by
the Compensation Committee. Under the category of income, the goals include one
or several of the following:&#160; pre-tax
income, earnings per share and net income. Under the category of balance sheet
management, the goals include one or several of the following criteria:&#160; shareholder equity, long-term debt to capital
ratio, investment rating, debt coverage, cash flow and return on invested
capital. The President and Chief Executive Officer is eligible to earn up to
100% of his base salary for meeting target goals and up to an additional 50% of
base salary for exceeding target goals. Twenty percent of his incentive bonus
is payable in restricted stock that vests ratably in equal amounts over a three
year period. The percentage incentive bonus opportunity for other executive
positions varies depending on their responsibility level. The amount actually
earned depends on each participant&#146;s position, bonus opportunity and actual
performance versus the pre-established goals.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Long-Term
Incentive Opportunities</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The long-term incentive program
consists of stock options and/or restricted stock awards granted under the AAR
CORP. Stock Benefit Plan.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Stock option awards typically
expire ten years from the date of grant or earlier upon termination of
employment, become exercisable in equal increments over a period of three to
five years on successive grant anniversary dates at the NYSE closing stock
price on the date of grant or, in some instances, upon meeting certain share
price performance criteria, and are accompanied by reload features. Typically,
stock option grants vest in 20% increments ratably on the grant date
anniversary over a five year period (Fiscal Year 2003 option grants had a dual
vesting schedule that also provided an opportunity for accelerated vesting
based on the Company&#146;s rolling 20-day average New York Stock Exchange stock
price appreciating above the grant price beyond certain specified threshold
values on a sliding scale). Restrictions imposed on restricted stock awards
vary and are designed, </font></p>

<font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;">
 <p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;line-height:9.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">10</p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">

<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=13,EFW="2115196",CP="AAR CORP",DN="1",CHK=495394,FOLIO='10',FILE="DISK027:[03CHI4.03CHI3744.EDGAR]DM3744.CHC",USER="AGAETZ",CD='Jul 23 13:35 2003' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">among other things, to encourage
executives to stay with the Company and to maintain a focus on long-term
objectives of the Company. Restricted stock grants vest over three to ten
years, depending on the grant; restrictions on restricted stock used in lieu of
cash to pay earned bonuses vests ratably over a three-year period. Typically,
awards are subject to forfeiture if the employee terminates employment for any
reason other than death, retirement or disability or the Company terminates
employment for cause, during the award cycle. During the award cycle the
participant receives dividends on the restricted shares and also has the right
to vote the restricted shares.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In determining stock option and
restricted stock awards, the Committee considers the recipient&#146;s position and
responsibilities in the Company, performance and contributions made during the
preceding year, capabilities and potential for future contribution to the
Company, the number of options and awards previously granted to the recipient
and, for senior management, their progress toward achieving the Company&#146;s
guidelines for stock ownership by senior management.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Board believes that Mr.&nbsp;Storch,
as the President and Chief Executive Officer, should have the opportunity,
based on performance, to become a significant stockholder and that the
performance measures that govern his opportunities should be both economic and
stockholder value related. Such measures should also be related to the Company&#146;s
industry and investor communities and reflect business objectives of the
Company over the coming years.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under a long-term incentive plan
approved by the Board and approved by the stockholders with respect to
performance restricted stock grants under this plan, commencing on June&nbsp;1,
2001 and ending on May&nbsp;31, 2005, Mr.&nbsp;Storch has the opportunity to
receive annually under the AAR CORP. Stock Benefit Plan, at the discretion of
the Compensation Committee, (i)&nbsp;options in an amount determined by a
fraction, the numerator of which is equal to 1.25 times his then current base
salary and the denominator of which is equal to the fair market value of the
common stock on the date of grant divided by three, and (ii)&nbsp;performance
restricted stock in amounts (a)&nbsp;up to .9375 times his then current base
salary based on the Company&#146;s average return on capital during the performance
period as compared to the S&amp;P 500 Composite average return on capital and (b)&nbsp;up
to .9375 times his then current base salary based on the Company&#146;s common stock
share price performance during the period as compared to the common stock share
price performance of the Company&#146;s peer group as described in the Company &#145;s
Proxy Statement.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Mr.&nbsp;Storch
and other named executive officers in the Summary Compensation Table below
received the stock options and restricted stock awards reflected in the tables
below. The number of shares covered by each grant reflects individual
contributions and performance, as well as competitive industry practices, in
the view of the Compensation Committee. The grant levels also continue the
Board&#146;s emphasis on executive stock ownership and further the Company&#146;s
objectives of tying incentive compensation to performance and aligning
executive&#146;s interests with the interests of the Company&#146;s stockholders.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Chief
Executive Officer Compensation</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In Fiscal 2002, Mr.&nbsp;Storch&#146;s
annual base salary was temporarily reduced effective October&nbsp;1, 2001, by
10%, or $69,628, as part of a Company-wide cost reduction effort following the
events of September&nbsp;11th. Effective May&nbsp;2, 2002, the Company
reinstated half of the salary reduction, or $34,814, as part of a Company-wide
salary reinstatement action. Mr.&nbsp;Storch&#146;s salary was unchanged in Fiscal
2003 and is presently $661,466. Mr.&nbsp;Storch received no Fiscal 2003
incentive bonus.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
tables which follow this report and accompanying footnotes and narrative
reflect the decisions covered by the above discussion.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Federal
Income Tax Considerations</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">IRC Section&nbsp;162(m)
generally prevents any public company from claiming a deduction for
compensation in excess of $1 million for the Chief Executive Officer or any of
the four highest </font></p>

<font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:black;font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;">
 <p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;line-height:9.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">11</p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">

<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=14,EFW="2115196",CP="AAR CORP",DN="1",CHK=942652,FOLIO='11',FILE="DISK027:[03CHI4.03CHI3744.EDGAR]DM3744.CHC",USER="AGAETZ",CD='Jul 23 13:35 2003' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">compensated
executive officers. This deduction limitation, however, does not apply to
performance-based compensation that satisfies certain requirements under Section&nbsp;162(m).
The Compensation Committee has determined that it is in the best interests of
the Company and its stockholders to structure compensation of executive
officers so that compensation will not be subject to the deduction limit to the
extent that it can reasonably do so in a manner that provides adequate
incentives and allows the Company to attract and retain qualified executives. However,
the Compensation Committee has previously and may in the future structure
compensation arrangements that under certain circumstances may be subject to
the deduction limit. None of the compensation paid by the Company in Fiscal
2003 was subject to the deduction limit.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Compensation Committee</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 10.15pt;text-indent:-10.15pt;"><sup><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:8.0pt;">1</font></sup><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="1" style="font-size:8.0pt;">On May 31, 2003, the following shares of restricted
stock were held by each named executive: Mr. Storch, 3,041; Mr. Pulsifer,
12,247; Mr. Romenesko, 22,745; Mr. Clark, 11,800; and Mr. Sharp, 3,169.&#160; The May 31, 2003 market value of each named
executive&#146;s restricted stock is as follows:&#160;
Mr. Storch, $13,685; Mr. Pulsifer, $55,112; Mr. Romenesko, $102,353; Mr.
Clark, $53,100; and Mr. Sharp, $14,261.&#160;
Vesting of restricted stock awards for executive officers varies from
three years for Mr. Storch to seven years for Fiscal Years 1999, 2000 and 2001
awards and ten years for Fiscal 1998 awards for other executive officers.&#160; Dividends are paid on all shares of
restricted stock.&#160; In the event of a
change in control of the Company as defined in the Plan, all restricted stock
awards become vested immediately.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 10.15pt;text-indent:-10.15pt;"><sup><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:8.0pt;">2</font></sup><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="1" style="font-size:8.0pt;">&#147;All Other Compensation&#148; includes the following:&#160; (i) contributions to the Company&#146;s 401(k)
plan on behalf of each of the named executives as a Company match of 2003
pre-tax elective deferred employee contributions: Mr. Storch, $2,000; Mr.
Pulsifer, $700; Mr. Romenesko, $800; Mr. Clark, $900; Mr. Sharp, $600; (ii) the
premium paid on group term life insurance for Mr. Pulsifer, $4,400; Mr.
Romenesko, $1,200; Mr. Clark, $500; Mr. Sharp, $400; and (iii) the value of the
benefit of the remainder of the premium paid under the Company&#146;s split dollar
life insurance program in the following amounts:&#160; Mr. Storch, $87,100; Mr. Pulsifer, $30,700;
Mr. Romenesko, $12,700; Mr. Clark, $5,700; Mr. Sharp, $7,100.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 10.15pt;text-indent:-10.15pt;"><sup><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:8.0pt;">3</font></sup><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="1" style="font-size:8.0pt;">Bonus
compensation was paid to Mr. Storch 80% in cash and 20% in restricted stock,
and to all others, 90% in cash and 10% in restricted stock, based on NYSE May
31 closing price each year.&#160; The
restricted stock vests over a three year period (one-third each grant anniversary
date).&#160; Dividends are paid on all shares
of restricted stock.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><a name="stockoptions"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">STOCK
OPTIONS</font></b></a></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Options generally become exercisable
20% each year over a five-year period. Unexercised options expire ten years
after the date of grant (Fiscal Year 2003 option grants were subject to a dual
vesting schedule that also provided an opportunity for accelerated vesting
based on the Company&#146;s rolling 20-day average New York Stock Exchange stock
price appreciating above the grant price beyond certain specified values on a
sliding scale). The stock option exercise price is equal to the fair market
value (NYSE closing price) of a share of stock on the date of grant. The
options have no value unless the stock price appreciates and the holder
satisfies the applicable vesting requirements.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
following table shows certain information with respect to stock options granted
in Fiscal 2003 to the named executive officers. It also shows how much the
named executive officers potentially may realize under two hypothetical
situations:&#160; if the stock gains 5% or 10%
in value per year compounded over the ten-year life of the options. These are
assumed hypothetical rates of appreciation required to be shown by Securities
Exchange Commission regulations as an example and are not a forecast of future
stock price appreciation.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Option Grants in Last Fiscal
Year</font></b></p>

<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><a name="pension"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">PENSION
BENEFITS</font></b></a></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Qualified
Plan Benefits</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company provides benefits to
all domestic employees including the named executive officers under a qualified
retirement program that includes defined benefits (The AAR CORP. Retirement
Plan, a cash balance type plan) and 401(k)/profit sharing plan (The AAR CORP.
Retirement Savings Plan). The defined benefits are based upon the present value
of a participant&#146;s benefit as of December&nbsp;31, 1999 and a formula for
benefits earned from and after January&nbsp;1, 2000 which takes into
consideration the participant&#146;s age, years of credited service, a percentage of
the participant&#146;s compensation for the year and certain interest credits. &#160;Compensation includes cash compensation shown
as income on an employee&#146;s Form&nbsp;W-2, reduced by certain items specified in
the plans, plus elective pre-tax contributions under the AAR CORP. Retirement
Savings Plan. Compensation for purposes of the qualified plans cannot exceed an
annual compensation limitation of $200,000 as adjusted from time to time by the
Commissioner of Internal Revenue in accordance with applicable provisions of
the IRC.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The aggregate salary and bonus compensation shown for
the named executive officers in the Summary Compensation Table above is the
compensation currently included for purposes of determining benefits under
qualified plans, subject to applicable IRC compensation limits for qualified
plans. Profit sharing and 401(k) benefits are based on elective pre-tax
contributions by employees with a Company match of up to 1 percentage point of
the first 5 percentage points of elective pre-tax contributions to the plan,
and a profit sharing contribution by the Company based on the individual
employee&#146;s elective pre-tax contributions and the economic performance of the
individual employee&#146;s operating unit. The Company has temporarily suspended its
Company matching contribution. The Company&#146;s profit sharing contribution can be
up to 3% of cash compensation.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Non-Qualified
Plan Benefits</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company provides
supplemental retirement benefits to certain executives and key employees under
the Supplemental Key Employee Retirement Plan (&#147;SKERP&#148;). &#160;All of the named executive officers are
participants in the SKERP. The SKERP is designed to restore the approximate
amount of benefits under the Company&#146;s qualified retirement savings plan lost
as a result of IRC limitations, including those limiting compensation for
purposes of benefit calculations. The SKERP also provides for aggregate
retirement benefits (including qualified plan benefits) at 60% and 50% of final
average compensation (as defined in plan documents), respectively, for the
President and Chief Executive Officer, and for certain other executive officers
designated by the Board, including three of the named executive officers,
reduced by certain items specified in plan documents. SKERP benefits are
unfunded and Company contributions and Supplemental Retirement benefits payable
by the Company are forfeited if the participant violates a covenant not to
compete set forth in the plan document or if employment is terminated for cause
(except that a forfeiture will not occur under certain circumstances in the
event of a change in control as defined in the plan document).</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Table of
Pension Benefits</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The following table shows the estimated aggregate
annual benefits payable upon retirement at normal retirement age (65) and years
of service for each of the named executive officers under the AAR CORP.
Retirement Plan and SKERP.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Pension Benefit Table</font></b></p>

<table border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="border-collapse:collapse;">
 <tr>
  <td width="31" valign="bottom" style="border:none;border-bottom:solid windowtext 1.0pt;padding:0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt;width:23.0pt;">
  <p align="left" style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:left;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:8.0pt;">Name</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="7" valign="bottom" style="padding:0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt 0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt;width:5.0pt;">
  <p style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:1.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="337" valign="bottom" style="padding:0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt 0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt;width:253.0pt;">
  <p style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:1.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="16" valign="bottom" style="padding:0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt 0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt;width:12.0pt;">
  <p style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:1.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="84" colspan="4" valign="bottom" style="border:none;border-bottom:solid windowtext 1.0pt;padding:0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt;width:62.75pt;">
  <p style="font-size:8.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:8.0pt;">Projected&nbsp;Annual<br>
  Benefit&nbsp;</font><font face="Times New Roman" style="font-family:Times New Roman;">at&nbsp;Age&nbsp;65</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="16" valign="bottom" style="padding:0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt 0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt;width:12.0pt;">

 <p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;line-height:9.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;">15</p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">

<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=18,EFW="2115196",CP="AAR CORP",DN="1",CHK=228439,FOLIO='15',FILE="DISK027:[03CHI4.03CHI3744.EDGAR]DQ3744.CHC",USER="AGAETZ",CD='Aug 11 16:10 2003' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><a name="agreements"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">EMPLOYMENT AND OTHER AGREEMENTS</font></b></a></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">David P. Storch</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has an employment
agreement with Mr.&nbsp;Storch designed to assure his continued services with
the Company at a base compensation of $661,466 per year or such increased
amount as the Board may determine. Mr.&nbsp;Storch&#146;s term of employment is
continuously extended so as to have a remaining term of three years, but shall
expire upon death, disability, retirement or other termination of employment.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Mr.&nbsp;Storch&#146;s employment
agreement also includes:&#160; confidentiality
and non-compete provisions; participation in the Company&#146;s benefit plans; a
severance payment upon termination of employment by the Company for other than
cause prior to a change in control of the Company equal to two times base
salary then in effect; a severance payment equal to three times his average
cash compensation (base salary plus cash bonus) for the last two fiscal years
of employment upon termination of employment under certain circumstances in the
event of a change in control of the Company; an incentive bonus opportunity of up
to 150% of base salary subject to annual financial targets approved by the
Compensation Committee (20% of any bonus is payable in three year restricted
stock); an annual long-term incentive stock compensation plan consisting of (i)&nbsp;an
annual option grant opportunity of an amount determined by a fraction, the
numerator of which is equal to 1.25 times his base salary and the denominator
of which is equal to the fair market value of the stock on the grant date
divided by three, and (ii)&nbsp;Performance Restricted Stock in amounts (a)&nbsp;up
to .9375 times his then current salary based on the Company&#146;s average return on
capital during the performance period as compared to the S&amp;P 500 Composite
average return on capital and (b)&nbsp;up to .9375 times his then current base salary
based on the Company&#146;s common stock share price performance during the period
as compared to the common stock share price performance of the Company&#146;s peer
group as described in the Company&#146;s Proxy Statement; a supplemental cash
payment to the extent necessary to preserve the level of benefits provided for
in the employment agreement in the event of imposition of excise taxes in
respect of &#147;excess parachute payments&#148; under the IRC and, in the event of a
change in control of the Company as defined in the employment agreement,
accelerated vesting of awards outstanding under the Company&#146;s Stock Benefit
Plan and continuation of certain other benefits for a period of three years.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.1pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.1pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Other
Agreements</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has entered into
severance agreements with certain key employees, including the named executive
officers other than Mr.&nbsp;Storch. The severance agreements are substantially
identical, include confidentiality and non-compete covenants, and provide for
payment of compensation and certain benefits in the event of termination of
employment for other than cause, including a change in control of the Company
as defined in the severance agreements. Severance equal to base salary plus any
earned incentive cash bonus will be paid upon termination of employment by the
Company for other than cause as defined in the severance agreements prior to a
change in control of the Company. Under certain circumstances, upon termination
of employment following a change in control, the employee will receive
severance equal to from one to three times total compensation (base salary plus
annual cash bonus) for the most recently ended fiscal year or the preceding
fiscal year, whichever is greater, accelerated vesting of awards outstanding
under the Company&#146;s Stock Benefit Plan, special supplemental retirement
benefits determined as if the employee had three additional years of service
under the Company&#146;s retirement plans, continuation of certain other benefits
for a period of three years, and a supplemental cash payment to the extent necessary
to preserve the level of benefits provided for in the severance agreement in
the event of imposition on such employee of excise taxes payable in respect of &#147;excess
parachute payments&#148; under the IRC.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has also entered
into split dollar life insurance agreements with certain key employees,
including three of the named executive officers. Under the agreements, the
Company will fund the annual insurance premiums for the policies subject to
reimbursement from the cash value or death benefit proceeds of the policies.</font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;line-height:9.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;">16</p>
</div><br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="black" align="center">
